                         {
                              "title": "Workaround for ky-universal not being able to be used with Jest",
                              "description": "This is not a bug report or an issue with ky-universal. \r\nI'm sharing a solution to a problem I had, hoping it would be visible to people having the same problem if I put it here. \r\nI'd be glad to move it to somewhere else if this is not the best place to share this.\r\n\r\n### TLDR;\r\nI wasn't able to import `ky-universal` in a Jest test file. \r\nI worked around this by creating the following file:\r\n`jest.setup.js`:\r\n```js\r\nconst fetch = require('node-fetch');\r\n\r\nglobalThis.fetch = fetch;\r\nglobalThis.Request = fetch.Request;\r\nglobalThis.Headers = fetch.Headers;\r\n```\r\n\r\nAnd adding this to `jest.config.js`:\r\n```js\r\nmodule.exports = {\r\n   ...\r\n   setupFiles: [\"./jest.setup.js\"],\r\n   ...\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\n### More details\r\n\r\n`ky-universal` is an ES6 module.  \r\nNo matter how hard I tried, I was not able to make Jest load an ES6 module. \r\nIt got transformed to something like this, probably by Babel:\r\n```\r\n ({\"Object.<anonymous>\":function(module,exports,require,__dirname,__filename,global,jest){import ky from \"ky\";\r\n ```\r\n And imports can't be anywhere except at the top level in ES6 Modules.\r\n \r\n With `ky`, I was able to get it transformed to `cjs` by installing `esbuild`:\r\n ```yarn add -D esbuild esbuild-jest```\r\n and adding this in my `jest.config.js`:\r\n ```js\r\nmodule.exports = {\r\n    ...\r\n    transform: {\r\n      \"^.+\\\\.(t|j)sx?$\": [\r\n        \"esbuild-jest\",\r\n        {}\r\n      ],\r\n    },\r\n    transformIgnorePatterns: [\r\n      '/node_modules/(?!ky)'\r\n    ]\r\n    ...\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\nBut `ky-universal` is doing top-level await inside it, and neither `esbuild-jest` nor `ts-jest` was able to process top level await.\r\n\r\nI tried so hard to make this work with just ES6 support and not using a bundler like esbuild. But I had to conclude this is pretty much impossible after two days of digging.\r\n\r\nSo I tried to start with just `ky`, which works fine when converted into `cjs` by `esbuild`, and started putting stuff into `globalThis`, one by one, by looking at the errors that came up.\r\n\r\nFor my code, errors stopped appearing after I assigned the above three things, but there could be more.\r\nIf it happens just check the error to see what's missing and add it to `globalThis`.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n   ",

                              "title": "fetch and electron renderer fail",
                              "description": "In a electron renderer thread if you don't bundle (nodeIntegration===true) you get whatever main prop a package points to, in this case we get the node version of ky. \r\n\r\nBut if we look at these lines https://github.com/sindresorhus/ky-universal/blob/master/index.js#L14-L16 we will get into troubles because the if clause tests if `global.fetch` exists and in electron renderer that will be true because native web fetch is available. \r\n\r\nSo instead of using node-fetch we use native fetch, but when another package using `ky` uses https://github.com/form-data/form-data with fetch it fails because `form-data` only works with node-fetch.\r\n\r\nTo fix this either we detect the environment for this specific case and workaround it or we remove the if clauses since `ky` already allows for lazy resolution of globals.\r\n\r\nI'm happy to PR a fix, but would like some feedback on this first.",

                              "title": "Pass url from partial",
                              "description": "Say you have a bunch of requests that you define like this:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nlet test = partial`\r\n    url: /auth/login\r\n    method: POST\r\n    body: ${{ email, password }}\r\n  `\r\n```\r\nrelative paths.\r\n\r\nIt would be awesome to do: \r\n\r\n```js\r\nlet response = await test`\r\n      url: ${url => `${process.env.API}/${url}`}\r\n      headers: ${{\r\n        Authorization: 'Bearer: token'\r\n      }}\r\n    `\r\n```\r\nThis way you can prefix urls and get the url from the partial.\r\n\r\nHere's the full example of what I'm doing in case you're curious\r\n```js\r\nimport base from 'requests/base'\r\nimport { partial } from 'legible'\r\n\r\nexport async function login({ email, password }) {\r\n  let request = partial`\r\n    url: /auth/login\r\n    method: POST\r\n    body: ${{ email, password }}\r\n  `\r\n\r\n  return await base(request)\r\n}\r\n\r\n//requests/base.js\r\n\r\nexport default async function request(partial) {\r\n  try {\r\n    let response = await partial`\r\n      url: ${url => `${process.env.API}/${url}`}\r\n      headers: ${{\r\n        Authorization: 'Bearer: token'\r\n      }}\r\n    `\r\n    return { response }\r\n  }\r\n  catch(error) {\r\n    console.log(error)\r\n    return { error }\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n\r\n```\r\n\r\nThis way I don't need to try catch everywhere and I can check for `error` on all requests. @raygesualdo ",

                         {
                              "title": "catching errors requires await even when calling synchronous functions with emit",
                              "description": "**EDIT:** I created a pull request with a one-line fix that doesn't break anything. A merge would be appreciated!\r\n\r\n```\r\nconst EventEmitter = require('events-async')\r\nconst eventEmitter = new EventEmitter()\r\n\r\nasync function asyncFunction() {\r\n    throw new Error('Async function error')\r\n}\r\n\r\neventEmitter.on('callAsyncFunction', asyncFunction)\r\n\r\nconst runAsyncFunction = async() => {\r\n    try {\r\n        await eventEmitter.emit('callAsyncFunction')\r\n    } catch(e) {\r\n        console.log(e)\r\n    }\r\n}\r\n\r\nrunAsyncFunction() // Works as expected and prints 'Async function error'.\r\n\r\n\r\nfunction syncFunction() {\r\n    throw new Error('Sync function error')\r\n}\r\n\r\neventEmitter.on('callSyncFunction', syncFunction) \r\n\r\ntry {\r\n    eventEmitter.emit('callSyncFunction') // Needs await if I want to catch the error even though it is calling a sync function to work as expected.\r\n} catch(e) {\r\n    console.log(e)\r\n}\r\n// Unhandled Promise Rejection. Requires await before eventEmitter.emit('callSyncFunction') even though calling sync function to allow it to catch the error.\r\n```\r\nRight now I am using the in-built node eventEmitter for synchronous functions and this one for async functions. If this is fixed, I can simply use this emitter and not use the in-built one at all.\r\n\r\nThe fix for this is actually simple since you are directly inheriting from the `eventEmitter` class. Instead of overriding its default `emit` method, let it be as is and rename your `emit` method to something else like `emitAsync` OR if you do not want to rename it, allow `emit` to accept an argument that allows it to run the default `emit` function. Another option is to set a variable `emitSync` to be equal to `emit` (the default one) before you override it. The idea is to allow the default `emit` method from the `events` module to be accessible as well for the purpose of synchronous events.\r\n\r\nThanks for your work!",

                              "title": "Problem with exception handling",
                              "description": "Your package works great - however, I'm now trying to figure out how to do proper error handling when for example the database goes down. And I run into what I think is a systematic issue with the use of async ... await on the one hand and try ... catch on the other hand as implemented in this package.\r\n\r\nThe issue is is described here:\r\nhttps://stackoverflow.com/questions/62392989/why-does-this-function-throw-an-exception-that-cannot-be-caught\r\n\r\nI assumed the problem was with my code, but it appears to be with the code in the package **or** I don't understand how to use it properly. This issue was caused by `pool.query` giving an error (because I closed the database :)).\r\n\r\nThat causes a throw on line 505. This throw is not caught by `awaitQuery` itself, as the throw happens in an async function called by pool.query. It can as a result not be caught anywhere and kills node.js as a result. Which is not acceptable for me.\r\n\r\nThis would fix it:\r\n\r\n```\r\nthis.pool.query(query, (err, result) => {\r\n  if ( err ) {\r\n    reject( err );\r\n  } else {\r\n    resolve( result );\r\n  }\r\n});\r\n```\r\n\r\nThis causes the error to reject the promise, and as a result it can be caught using try catch in the code using `awaitQuery`:\r\n\r\n```\r\ntry {\r\n  const rows = await dbPool.awaitQuery(`SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = '${id}'`);\r\n  [user = null] = rows;\r\n  return user;\r\n} catch (error) {\r\n  console.log('database error');\r\n  return null;\r\n}\r\n\r\n```\r\nSo, am I not understanding how I should use this code, or is this a legitimate issue that can be fixed in the package?",

                         {
                              "title": "Special '/' char in a DOMFile name is required by W3C specs to be automatically replaced with ':' ",
                              "description": "Starting from Firefox 53, any '/' special character in a DOMFile name is replaced with a ':' and this change has been required by the related W3C specs and it is explicitly tested in WPT tests:\r\n\r\n- [Bug 1321534 - File::Constructor should normalize the filename](https://bugzilla.mozilla.org/show_bug.cgi?id=1321534)\r\n- [related WPT test](https://github.com/w3c/web-platform-tests/blob/a3bb0fc/FileAPI/file/File-constructor.html#L43)\r\n\r\nIn the current implementation, this change currently breaks the assumption that the File instance filename is the exact same string assigned through the File instance constructor, this means that the assigned name when the File has been saved in the IndexedDB and the one the we get when we retrieve the list of the saved files are not going to be the same on Firefox anymore (and also on Chrome once they will implement the behavior tested by the WPT).\r\n\r\nA reasonable solution is probably to change the API of the idb-file-storage library and make the `fileStorage.put(...)` filename parameter always mandatory, so that when we save the file we never use the \"normalized\" filename of File instance as the default filename in the IndexedDB index.\r\n \r\nNOTE: Chrome doesn't seem to implement this behavior yet, but given that is tested explicitly in the WPT tests, this is likely to change also on chrome in the future.
